When we approach some new area of phenomena and are completely clueless, we start with feeling and intuitions, doubts and conjectures, which gradually crystallize into a philosophical framework. If the framework is useful, it gives way gradually to science, which involves both more formal reasoning and more quantitative empiricism. And this serves as the foundation for technology.Philosophy in the sense of doubt, of swirling conjectures, of speculation, characterizes much human activity. When a master mechanic looks at a malfunctioning car engine and strives to narrow down what could be wrong, various hypotheses will be going through his mind and he will attempt to test them. Likewise for a physician attempting a diagnosis. Likewise for a computer programmer trying to figure out what‚Äôs wrong with a complex program.The problem with modern philosophy is it has become a meal ticket for professional academics who have a vested material interest in nonstop chatter. The racket of professional academic philosophy is what pays their mortgage. This nonstop and overly technical, vacuous, obfuscating, and inconclusive chatter is what turns a lot of people off.
CorkyAgain #464176 June 27, 2025 11:35 am 6

Arshad Ali #463920 June 26, 2025 11:57 am 8
I learnt a fair bit from philosophy myself. Around 500 BC, there was the birth of abstract reasoning with the pre-Socratics. Good, evil, the nature of reality, the ideal form of governance ‚Äî all as abstract ideas. And as abstract ideas we need to discuss and define what they should mean. This is why, from a historical point of view at least, Plato‚Äôs dialogues are interesting. Other than the ancient Greek philosophers, I learnt a fair bit from Kant‚Äôs ‚ÄúCritique of Pure Reason,‚Äù which is analogous to an intensive gym workout. Among modern writers I‚Äôm smitten with Magee‚Äôs ‚ÄúConfessions of a Philosopher.‚Äù As postscript add Pirsig‚Äôs Zen and the Art of Motorcycle Maintenance.‚Äù

After the revolution of Kant, philosophy became problematic.Sorry, again adding as a postscript (I‚Äôm in the middle of cooking my next meal). Texts on logic and rhetoric will sharpen your thinking, allow you to distinguish more clearly between meretricious and sound arguments. Which reflects the ancient antagonism between teachers of philosophy and teachers of rhetoric. As far as I know, Aristotle was the first to enumerate and describe forms of sound reasoning, though Aristotelian logic gave way over a century back to symbolic logic, which morphed into today‚Äôs mathematical logic. This field is much more technical and extensive than anything Aristotle could have dreamt of. Which reminds me that Bell and Machover‚Äôs ‚ÄúA Course in Mathematical Logic‚Äù is one of my favorite texts. Though I see Manin has a more recent book. Still, I must pay homage to Aristotle as the founder and forerunner, just as mathematicians pay homage to Euclid, Pythagoras, and Diophantus.

CFOmally #464443 June 28, 2025 2:36 pm 48
I thought I‚Äôd share with everyone an email he sent me a few months ago. I asked him how the heck he cranks out so much material and holds down a career, his answer:‚ÄúWhenever anyone asks about writing, my first bit of advice is something I read in a biography of William Falkner. He wrote two novels in the style of the lost generation that was popular at the time, but they did not sell. An editor suggested he write about things he knows and cares about. The result was The Sound and the Fury. He spent the rest of his life writing about what he knew.In my case, I stick to what I like and I write for myself. I am the only audience that matters. Every day I write¬†an essay to myself about whatever is on my mind.The second bit of advice is to write every day like it is a job. I get up every morning knowing I will write for an hour or two. I think if I retire from the day job, the schedule will be write in the morning for a few hours, then go outside and do chores. Have lunch and write some more in the afternoon. Audio and video will be evening things. That way, I have a routine.As far as how I write, I just start writing about something and let my mind wander as I do it. More often than not just typing it out leads to either a bigger idea or, sometimes, a totally new idea. I keep a list of ideas that pop into my head, but the list just grows and grows, so once a month I read through it and trim it back. A lot of my ideas turn out to be quite silly or even stupid.I know a guy who writes fiction and his method is to write in a way that will describe the person he has in mind. Therefore, the plot and scenery serve to explain the character, which leads to coming up with creative setting for his characters. If I ever write fiction, that is how I would go about it. Treat the characters as puzzles to solve by placing them into situations that reveal their nature.¬†I like reading stuff like that.I do very little editing. I run it through Word, but that is it. Instead, I set limits. Short sentences, short paragraphs and about 1000 words in total for a post. This makes for more reader friendly copy and keeps me from meandering. I went to Jesuit schools and they always told us, our writing should be like a woman‚Äôs bathing suit. Long enough to cover the important parts, but short enough to be interesting.In the end, the best place to start is to just start writing and see where it takes you.Z‚ÄùPerhaps it will encourage others to writeCFO

Best known for his ‚ÄúSkinner Box‚Äù experiment/concept, he touched upon why we act as we do. His revelation in short,‚ÄúWe are not free to choose; we are products of our environment and history of reinforcement.‚ÄùA very enticing concept, except when you delved more deeply into explaining any particular human action beyond the simplest ‚Äústimulus-response‚Äù paradigm. The complexity of describing all possible stimulus inputs producing the observed response was overwhelming. From there it was a short trip into the pseudo scientific world of Freudianism.I left the course thinking that Skinner may very well have been correct, but his explanation of the ultimate cause of human behavior was simply too complex to be useful. As Z-man ponders in today‚Äôs missive, an incorrect, but simple/workable understanding might be more useful than a correct, but complex/theoretical understanding of human behavior.

Arguments that free will doesn‚Äôt exist are like arguments that bananas don‚Äôt exist. They start either by leaving the term ‚Äúfree will‚Äù undefined or by slipping in a philosophical definition that requires human action to be totally un-caused by prior events. Then they conclude,presto!, that free will doesn‚Äôt exist. You can use exactly the same argument to prove that bananas don‚Äôt exist.In fact, we all experience and exhibit behavior that we call ‚Äúfree will.‚Äù The only question is how best to define the reality that‚Äôs right in front of us. We can quibble about it, but the most defensible definition is some version of the libertarian: if coercion is not involved, then we act freely.

It is an old French word and used by the English in medieval times. It means simply, ‚Äúfarmhand‚Äù or ‚Äúperson of the village (villa)‚Äù. Basically referred to a lower class peasant who was one with no landholdings. Later on, the term became a perjoritive as it ‚Äúbegan to be associated with crude, dishonest, or untrustworthy behavior. Eventually, in English, it evolved into its modern meaning of a morally corrupt or evil person.‚Äù (ChatGPT)I first ran across this distinction in Steven Pinker‚Äôs book, ‚ÄúThe Better Angels of Our Nature: Why Violence Has Declined (2011).‚Äù In this book Pinker argues for a rapid decline in violence because of increased death rate (mainly due to execution/punishment) of violent individuals in merry old England. Dar Mr. Sir,REQUEST FOR ASSISTANCE-STRICTLY CONFIDENTIALI am Dr. Bakare Tunde, the cousin of Nigerian Astronaut, Air Force Major Abacha Tunde. He was the first African in space when he made a secret flight to the Salyut 6 space station in 1979. He was on a later Soviet spaceflight, Soyuz T-16Z to the secret Soviet military space station Salyut 8T in 1989.He was stranded there in 1990 when the Soviet Union was dissolved. His other Soviet crew members returned to earth on the Soyuz T-16Z, but his place was taken up by return cargo. There have been occasional Progrez supply flights to keep him going since that time. He is in good humor, but wants to come home.In the 14-years since he has been on the station, he has accumulated flight pay and interest amounting to almost $ 15,000,000 American Dollars. This is held in a trust at the Lagos National Savings and Trust Association. If we can obtain access to this money, we can place a down payment with the Russian Space Authorities for a Soyuz return flight to bring him back to Earth. I am told this will cost $ 3,000,000 American Dollars. In order to access his trust fund we need your assistance.Consequently, my colleagues and I are willing to transfer the total amount to your account or subsequent disbursement, since we as civil servants are prohibited by the Code of Conduct Bureau (Civil Service Laws) from opening and/ or operating foreign accounts in our names.Needless to say, the trust reposed on you at this juncture is enormous. In return, we have agreed to offer you 20 percent of the transferred sum, while 10 percent shall be set aside for incidental expenses (internal andexternal) between the parties in the course of the transaction. You will be mandated to remit the balance 70 percent to other accounts in due course.Kindly expedite action as we are behind schedule to enable us include downpayment in this financial quarter.Please acknowledge the receipt of this message via my direct number 234 (0) 9-234-2220 only.Yours Sincerely,Dr. Bakare Tunde Astronautics Project Manager

Dear Mr. Sir,REQUEST FOR ASSISTANCE-STRICTLY CONFIDENTIALI am Dr. Bakare Tunde, the cousin of Nigerian Astronaut, Air Force Major Abacha Tunde. He was the first African in space when he made a secret flight to the Salyut 6 space station in 1979. He was on a later Soviet spaceflight, Soyuz T-16Z to the secret Soviet military space station Salyut 8T in 1989.He was stranded there in 1990 when the Soviet Union was dissolved. His other Soviet crew members returned to earth on the Soyuz T-16Z, but his place was taken up by return cargo. There have been occasional Progrez supply flights to keep him going since that time. He is in good humor, but wants to come home.In the 14-years since he has been on the station, he has accumulated flight pay and interest amounting to almost $ 15,000,000 American Dollars. This is held in a trust at the Lagos National Savings and Trust Association. If we can obtain access to this money, we can place a down payment with the Russian Space Authorities for a Soyuz return flight to bring him back to Earth. I am told this will cost $ 3,000,000 American Dollars. In order to access his trust fund we need your assistance.Consequently, my colleagues and I are willing to transfer the total amount to your account or subsequent disbursement, since we as civil servants are prohibited by the Code of Conduct Bureau (Civil Service Laws) from opening and/ or operating foreign accounts in our names.Needless to say, the trust reposed on you at this juncture is enormous. In return, we have agreed to offer you 20 percent of the transferred sum, while 10 percent shall be set aside for incidental expenses (internal andexternal) between the parties in the course of the transaction. You will be mandated to remit the balance 70 percent to other accounts in due course.Kindly expedite action as we are behind schedule to enable us include downpayment in this financial quarter.Please acknowledge the receipt of this message via my direct number 234 (0) 9-234-2220 only.Yours Sincerely,Dr. Bakare Tunde Astronautics Project Manager

Dear Mr. Sir,REQUEST FOR ASSISTANCE-STRICTLY CONFIDENTIALI am Dr. Bakare Tunde, the cousin of Nigerian Astronaut, Air Force Major Abacha Tunde. He was the first African in space when he made a secret flight to the Salyut 6 space station in 1979. He was on a later Soviet spaceflight, Soyuz T-16Z to the secret Soviet military space station Salyut 8T in 1989.He was stranded there in 1990 when the Soviet Union was dissolved. His other Soviet crew members returned to earth on the Soyuz T-16Z, but his place was taken up by return cargo. There have been occasional Progrez supply flights to keep him going since that time. He is in good humor, but wants to come home.In the 14-years since he has been on the station, he has accumulated flight pay and interest amounting to almost $ 15,000,000 American Dollars. This is held in a trust at the Lagos National Savings and Trust Association. If we can obtain access to this money, we can place a down payment with the Russian Space Authorities for a Soyuz return flight to bring him back to Earth. I am told this will cost $ 3,000,000 American Dollars. In order to access his trust fund we need your assistance.Consequently, my colleagues and I are willing to transfer the total amount to your account or subsequent disbursement, since we as civil servants are prohibited by the Code of Conduct Bureau (Civil Serrvice Laws) from opening and/ or operating foreign accounts in our names.Needless to say, the trust reposed on you at this juncture is enormous. In return, we have agreed to offer you 20 percent of the transferred sum, while 10 percent shall be set aside for incidental expenses (internal andexternal) between the parties in the course of the transaction. You will be mandated to remit the balance 70 percent to other accounts in due course.Kindly expedite action as we are behind schedule to enable us include downpayment in this financial quarter.Please acknowledge the receipt of this message via my direct number 234 (0) 9-234-2220 only.Yours Sincerely,Dr. Bakare Tunde Astronautics Project Manager

Dear Mr. Sir,REQUEST FOR ASSISTANCE-STRICTLY CONFIDENTIALI am Dr. Bakare Tunde, the cousin of Nigerian Astronaut, Air Force Major Abacha Tunde. He was the first African in space when he made a secret flight to the Salyut 6 space station in 1979. He was on a later Soviet spaceflight, Soyuz T-16Z to the secret Soviet military space station Salyut 8T in 1989.He was stranded there in 1990 when the Soviet Union was dissolved. His other Soviet crew members returned to earth on the Soyuz T-16Z, but his place was taken up by return cargo. There have been occasional Progrez supply flights to keep him going since that time. He is in good humor, but wants to come home.In the 14-years since he has been on the station, he has accumulated flight pay and interest amounting to almost $ 15,000,000 American Dollars. This is held in a trust at the Lagos National Savings and Trust Association. If we can obtain access to this money, we can place a down payment with the Russian Space Authorities for a Soyuz return flight to bring him back to Earth. I am told this will cost $ 3,000,000 American Dollars. In order to access his trust fund we need your assistance.Consequently, my colleagues and I are willing to transfer the total amount to your account or subsequent disbursement, since we as civil servants are prohibited by the Code of Conduct Bureau (Civil Serrvice Laws) from opening and/ or operating foreign accounts in our names.Needless to say, the trust reposed on you at this juncture is enormous. In return, we have agreed to offer you 20 percent of the transferred sum, while 10 percent shall be set aside for incidental expenses (internal andexternal) between the parties in the course of the transaction. You will be mandated to remit the balance 70 percent to other accounts in due course.Kindly expedite action as we are behind schedule to enable us include downpayment in this financial quarter.Please acknowledge the receipt of this message via my direct number 234 (0) 9-234-2220 only.Yours Sincerely,Dr. Bakare Tunde Astronautics Project Manager

Michael Farris #464617 June 30, 2025 8:44 am -10
Dear Mr. Sir,REQUEST FOR ASSISTANCE-STRICTLY CONFIDENTIALI am Dr. Bakare Tunde, the cousin of Nigerian Astronaut, Air Force Major Abacha Tunde. He was the first African in space when he made a secret flight to the Salyut 6 space station in 1979. He was on a later Soviet spaceflight, Soyuz T-16Z to the secret Soviet military space station Salyut 8T in 1989.He was stranded there in 1990 when the Soviet Union was dissolved. His other Soviet crew members returned to earth on the Soyuz T-16Z, but his place was taken up by return cargo. There have been occasional Progrez supply flights to keep him going since that time. He is in good humor, but wants to come home.In the 14-years since he has been on the station, he has accumulated flight pay and interest amounting to almost $ 15,000,000 American Dollars. This is held in a trust at the Lagos National Savings and Trust Association. If we can obtain access to this money, we can place a down payment with the Russian Space Authorities for a Soyuz return flight to bring him back to Earth. I am told this will cost $ 3,000,000 American Dollars. In order to access his trust fund we need your assistance.Consequently, my colleagues and I are willing to transfer the total amount to your account or subsequent disbursement, since we as civil servants are prohibited by the Code of Conduct Bureau (Civil Serrvice Laws) from opening and/ or operating foreign accounts in our names.Needless to say, the trust reposed on you at this juncture is enormous. In return, we have agreed to offer you 20 percent of the transferred sum, while 10 percent shall be set aside for incidental expenses (internal andexternal) between the parties in the course of the transaction. You will be mandated to remit the balance 70 percent to other accounts in due course.Kindly expedite action as we are behind schedule to enable us include downpayment in this financial quarter.Please acknowledge the receipt of this message via my direct number 234 (0) 9-234-2220 only.Yours Sincerely,Dr. Bakare Tunde Astronautics Project Manager

Dear Mr. Sir,REQUEST FOR ASSISTANCE-STRICTLY CONFIDENTIALI am Dr. Bakare Tunde, the cousin of Nigerian Astronaut, Air Force Major Abacha Tunde. He was the first African in space when he made a secret flight to the Salyut 6 space station in 1979. He was on a later Soviet spaceflight, Soyuz T-16Z to the secret Soviet military space station Salyut 8T in 1989.He was stranded there in 1990 when the Soviet Union was dissolved. His other Soviet crew members returned to earth on the Soyuz T-16Z, but his place was taken up by return cargo. There have been occasional Progrez supply flights to keep him going since that time. He is in good humor, but wants to come home.In the 14-years since he has been on the station, he has accumulated flight pay and interest amounting to almost $ 15,000,000 American Dollars. This is held in a trust at the Lagos National Savings and Trust Association. If we can obtain access to this money, we can place a down payment with the Russian Space Authorities for a Soyuz return flight to bring him back to Earth. I am told this will cost $ 3,000,000 American Dollars. In order to access his trust fund we need your assistance.Consequently, my colleagues and I are willing to transfer the total amount to your account or subsequent disbursement, since we as civil servants are prohibited by the Code of Conduct Bureau (Civil Serrvice Laws) from opening and/ or operating foreign accounts in our names.Needless to say, the trust reposed on you at this juncture is enormous. In return, we have agreed to offer you 20 percent of the transferred sum, while 10 percent shall be set aside for incidental expenses (internal andexternal) between the parties in the course of the transaction. You will be mandated to remit the balance 70 percent to other accounts in due course.Kindly expedite action as we are behind schedule to enable us include downpayment in this financial quarter.Please acknowledge the receipt of this message via my direct number 234 (0) 9-234-2220 only.Yours Sincerely,Dr. Bakare Tunde Astronautics Project Manager
